					<p class="sbi_hover_caption_wrap"
		>
		<span
			class="sbi_caption">Fueling for Life (Not Shrinking It)<br><br>I almost didn’t share this essay.<br>Not because it isn’t true — but because I doubted myself.<br>Because I thought, who am I to say this?<br><br>And yet, I’ve learned that it’s often the very things we hesitate to share that need a voice the most.<br><br>This isn’t medical advice.<br>It’s lived experience.<br>Pattern recognition.<br>What I’ve seen in my own body — and in the bodies and lives of so many women around me.<br><br>Somewhere along the way, many of us learned to fear food.<br>To override hunger.<br>To believe being busy and under-fueled was strength.<br><br>I under-fueled for most of my life without even realizing it. I followed rules, subscribed to food fears, and thought I was doing everything “right.” In midlife, I realized I didn’t need more rules — I needed more support.<br><br>Fueling myself regularly has been one of the most grounding, healing things I’ve done for my body and my nervous system. Not perfectly — but consistently. Eating enough. Eating with less fear. Letting nourishment be steady instead of stressful.<br><br>This essay is about what chronic under-fueling and food fear do to us — and how nourishment, safety, and trust restore something much deeper than health.<br><br>It’s about so much more than food…<br>but food is where I begin.<br><br>If this resonates, I’d love for you to read the full blog post on my website.<br><br>Comment FUEL and I’ll send you the link 🤍<br><br>xoxo,<br>Jackie</span>

			<a class="sbi_link_area nofancybox" rel="nofollow noopener" href="https://scontent.cdninstagram.com/v/t51.82787-15/619544163_18550245817047435_4312970473529317156_n.jpg?stp=dst-jpg_e35_tt6&#038;_nc_cat=106&#038;ccb=7-5&#038;_nc_sid=18de74&#038;efg=eyJlZmdfdGFnIjoiRkVFRC5iZXN0X2ltYWdlX3VybGdlbi5DMyJ9&#038;_nc_ohc=CEA3E_qTyxAQ7kNvwHZPP0Y&#038;_nc_oc=AdnSTocqNJHo-SFfdXr9qysuIGBxgYqrUvA4W6nrwqQWbH9extUVJVuKQhxrc9GHp7Q&#038;_nc_zt=23&#038;_nc_ht=scontent.cdninstagram.com&#038;edm=ANo9K5cEAAAA&#038;_nc_gid=ukBEBY10icdh6asS1gggMg&#038;_nc_tpa=Q5bMBQGe3-xcv-u1tdVgVr2SZMh1mWezguko7HjJWO6MijbLyIpUgJeXA_zk47mFSRWsGzn1t50HDXuDOQ&#038;oh=00_AfvdREpaRse8mprBtU7_ESJLIUm2NF9hZnEQBOfAMWKs3A&#038;oe=69A200E4"
			   data-lightbox-sbi=""
			   data-title="Fueling for Life (Not Shrinking It)&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
I almost didn’t share this essay.&lt;br&gt;
Not because it isn’t true — but because I doubted myself.&lt;br&gt;
Because I thought, who am I to say this?&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
And yet, I’ve learned that it’s often the very things we hesitate to share that need a voice the most.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
This isn’t medical advice.&lt;br&gt;
It’s lived experience.&lt;br&gt;
Pattern recognition.&lt;br&gt;
What I’ve seen in my own body — and in the bodies and lives of so many women around me.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Somewhere along the way, many of us learned to fear food.&lt;br&gt;
To override hunger.&lt;br&gt;
To believe being busy and under-fueled was strength.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
I under-fueled for most of my life without even realizing it. I followed rules, subscribed to food fears, and thought I was doing everything “right.” In midlife, I realized I didn’t need more rules — I needed more support.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Fueling myself regularly has been one of the most grounding, healing things I’ve done for my body and my nervous system. Not perfectly — but consistently. Eating enough. Eating with less fear. Letting nourishment be steady instead of stressful.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
This essay is about what chronic under-fueling and food fear do to us — and how nourishment, safety, and trust restore something much deeper than health.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
It’s about so much more than food…&lt;br&gt;
but food is where I begin.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
If this resonates, I’d love for you to read the full blog post on my website.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Comment FUEL and I’ll send you the link 🤍&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
xoxo,&lt;br&gt;
Jackie"

		   tabindex="-1">
			<img src="https://marinmamacooks.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed-pro/img/placeholder.png" alt="Fueling for Life (Not Shrinking It)

I almost didn’t share this essay.
Not because it isn’t true — but because I doubted myself.
Because I thought, who am I to say this?

And yet, I’ve learned that it’s often the very things we hesitate to share that need a voice the most.

This isn’t medical advice.
It’s lived experience.
Pattern recognition.
What I’ve seen in my own body — and in the bodies and lives of so many women around me.

Somewhere along the way, many of us learned to fear food.
To override hunger.
To believe being busy and under-fueled was strength.

I under-fueled for most of my life without even realizing it. I followed rules, subscribed to food fears, and thought I was doing everything “right.” In midlife, I realized I didn’t need more rules — I needed more support.

Fueling myself regularly has been one of the most grounding, healing things I’ve done for my body and my nervous system. Not perfectly — but consistently. Eating enough. Eating with less fear. Letting nourishment be steady instead of stressful.

This essay is about what chronic under-fueling and food fear do to us — and how nourishment, safety, and trust restore something much deeper than health.

It’s about so much more than food…
but food is where I begin.

If this resonates, I’d love for you to read the full blog post on my website.

Comment FUEL and I’ll send you the link 🤍

xoxo,
Jackie">

			   data-lightbox-sbi=""
			   data-title="This morning it hit me:&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
I can’t see my old dream anymore.&lt;br&gt;
It’s gone.&lt;br&gt;
The version of me I spent years building toward — dissolving.&lt;br&gt;
The career vision I thought was “the dream” — fading out.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
And instead of panicking or forcing clarity,&lt;br&gt;
I’m letting myself be in the void.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Because the truth is…&lt;br&gt;
I don’t want a dream that fits inside one box anymore.&lt;br&gt;
I don’t want a single identity or one grand vision to chase.&lt;br&gt;
I don’t want to lock myself into a future my evolving self may outgrow.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Maybe the dream isn’t a destination.&lt;br&gt;
Maybe the dream is a frequency.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
What lights me up.&lt;br&gt;
What feels true.&lt;br&gt;
What feels alive.&lt;br&gt;
What feels honest today.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Maybe the dream is allowed to shift.&lt;br&gt;
Maybe it’s supposed to.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Today, my dream is simply to follow what feels real —&lt;br&gt;
and let the deeper vision reveal itself in its own timing.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
This carousel is the download that arrived from that space —&lt;br&gt;
the space between dreams,&lt;br&gt;
the quiet place where becoming begins.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
How many of you feel this transitional void this time of year?&lt;br&gt;
Winter has a way of pulling us inward — into reflection, softening, and deep listening.&lt;br&gt;
It’s a season for tending the unseen, resting, and sensing the new seeds we’re meant to grow next.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
If you’re in this in-between too… you’re exactly where you’re meant to be.&lt;br&gt;

			<img src="https://marinmamacooks.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed-pro/img/placeholder.png" alt="This morning it hit me:

I can’t see my old dream anymore.
It’s gone.
The version of me I spent years building toward — dissolving.
The career vision I thought was “the dream” — fading out.

And instead of panicking or forcing clarity,
I’m letting myself be in the void.

Because the truth is…
I don’t want a dream that fits inside one box anymore.
I don’t want a single identity or one grand vision to chase.
I don’t want to lock myself into a future my evolving self may outgrow.

Maybe the dream isn’t a destination.
Maybe the dream is a frequency.

What lights me up.
What feels true.
What feels alive.
What feels honest today.

Maybe the dream is allowed to shift.
Maybe it’s supposed to.

Today, my dream is simply to follow what feels real —
and let the deeper vision reveal itself in its own timing.

This carousel is the download that arrived from that space —
the space between dreams,
the quiet place where becoming begins.

How many of you feel this transitional void this time of year?
Winter has a way of pulling us inward — into reflection, softening, and deep listening.
It’s a season for tending the unseen, resting, and sensing the new seeds we’re meant to grow next.

If you’re in this in-between too… you’re exactly where you’re meant to be.

#attunedwoman #innerseason #voidseason #becoming">
		</a>

			<img src="https://marinmamacooks.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed-pro/img/placeholder.png" alt="The easiest way to turn random leftovers into a nourishing bowl of soup. This is my favorite soup to whip up when it’s cold and I’m craving something nourishing. It’s basically a 10-minute, high-protein bone broth soup you can make with whatever leftovers you already have in your fridge.

Kale, spinach, quinoa, rice, leftover turkey, ground beef, shredded chicken… it all works.

Warm your bone broth of choice, add some greens, add your protein, add your grain.
That’s it.
Simple, cozy, nourishing, and perfect for one.

Feeding a family? Just bump up the ingredients and make a big pot.

I make this anytime I want something grounding and done fast.
Save this for the next time you’re staring into your fridge wondering what to make.🩷

	<div class="sbi_inner_wrap" >

						<svg style="color: rgba(255,255,255,1)" class="svg-inline--fa fa-play fa-w-14 sbi_playbtn" aria-label="Play" aria-hidden="true" data-fa-processed="" data-prefix="fa" data-icon="play" role="presentation" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 448 512"><path fill="currentColor" d="M424.4 214.7L72.4 6.6C43.8-10.3 0 6.1 0 47.9V464c0 37.5 40.7 60.1 72.4 41.3l352-208c31.4-18.5 31.5-64.1 0-82.6z"></path></svg>
		<div  style="background: rgba(0,0,0,0.85)"  class="sbi_link  sbi_disable_lightbox" >
			<div class="sbi_hover_top">

					<p class="sbi_hover_caption_wrap"
		>
		<span
			class="sbi_caption">Creamy Overnight Steel Cut Oats for One (5-Minute Prep)<br>Serves 1<br>I love making my breakfast at night, so my mornings feel grounded and calm. It takes the guesswork out of ‘what’s for breakfast?’ and this one takes under 5 minutes to prep — and just 5 minutes to heat up.<br><br>Ingredients<br>For the Porridge Base<br>• ½ cup unsweetened full-fat canned coconut milk <br>• ¼ cup unsweetened almond milk (or any milk you love) @threetreesfoods <br>• ½ tablespoon raw, smooth tahini<br>• ½ teaspoon cinnamon (I use Ceylon)<br>• 1 teaspoon pure maple syrup<br>• Pinch of pink Himalayan Sea salt<br>• ¼ cup gluten-free steel cut oats (or rolled oats)<br><br>Suggested Toppings<br>• Drizzle of tahini, almond butter, walnut butter, or peanut butter<br>• 1 cup frozen wild blueberries (thawed), or any berries<br>• Extra maple syrup<br>• Optional: bee pollen, hemp seeds, chia, or anything crunchy + nourishing<br><br>Instructions<br>Night Before<br>	1.	Combine: In a jar with a lid, add the coconut milk, almond milk, tahini, cinnamon, maple syrup, salt, and steel cut oats.<br>	2.	Shake: Seal and give it a good shake.<br>	3.	Chill: Refrigerate overnight to thicken.<br><br>Note: You can skip the maple syrup and tahini in the mixture if you prefer to add them as toppings — I often do this. The base can simply be milk, cinnamon, and salt.<br><br>Morning Of<br>	1.	Heat: Pour the porridge into a small saucepan over medium heat until warm. (Microwave works too if you’re short on time.)<br>	2.	Serve: Transfer to a bowl.<br>	3.	Top: Add berries, a drizzle of tahini or nut butter, maple syrup to taste, and any extras you love. The tahini + blueberries combo is heaven.<br><br>Save this so you can already wake up nourished and grounded. <br><br>#overnightoatsrecipe #overnightoats</span>
	</p>

			</div>

			<a class="sbi_link_area nofancybox" rel="nofollow noopener" href="https://scontent.cdninstagram.com/v/t51.82787-15/591125916_18540079087047435_9126717498865737234_n.jpg?stp=dst-jpg_e35_tt6&#038;_nc_cat=107&#038;ccb=7-5&#038;_nc_sid=18de74&#038;efg=eyJlZmdfdGFnIjoiQ0xJUFMuYmVzdF9pbWFnZV91cmxnZW4uQzMifQ%3D%3D&#038;_nc_ohc=A_Wr8YuNwwAQ7kNvwF87eH0&#038;_nc_oc=AdmOpgYVKGm8QRE9xqxkxEWw5R6clYDsLybcSdzlAfgkA91vkPz0JFGKI57KuK9rjvw&#038;_nc_zt=23&#038;_nc_ht=scontent.cdninstagram.com&#038;edm=ANo9K5cEAAAA&#038;_nc_gid=ukBEBY10icdh6asS1gggMg&#038;_nc_tpa=Q5bMBQFHVdGW9rxNPCJDVa1y31eZD1mTrdGlQLmHzmwxYMWunC2iSJIEpB8FRCsbBe9yCRBFEnlqTKJWOg&#038;oh=00_AfuKYjp9kVmXyMfN_wx23oA78PME5_gUqOroSxVuDDFU0w&#038;oe=69A1FBDD"
			   data-lightbox-sbi=""
			   data-title="Creamy Overnight Steel Cut Oats for One (5-Minute Prep)&lt;br&gt;
Serves 1&lt;br&gt;
I love making my breakfast at night, so my mornings feel grounded and calm. It takes the guesswork out of ‘what’s for breakfast?’ and this one takes under 5 minutes to prep — and just 5 minutes to heat up.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Ingredients&lt;br&gt;
For the Porridge Base&lt;br&gt;
• ½ cup unsweetened full-fat canned coconut milk &lt;br&gt;
• ¼ cup unsweetened almond milk (or any milk you love) @threetreesfoods &lt;br&gt;
• ½ tablespoon raw, smooth tahini&lt;br&gt;
• ½ teaspoon cinnamon (I use Ceylon)&lt;br&gt;
• 1 teaspoon pure maple syrup&lt;br&gt;
• Pinch of pink Himalayan Sea salt&lt;br&gt;
• ¼ cup gluten-free steel cut oats (or rolled oats)&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Suggested Toppings&lt;br&gt;
• Drizzle of tahini, almond butter, walnut butter, or peanut butter&lt;br&gt;
• 1 cup frozen wild blueberries (thawed), or any berries&lt;br&gt;
• Extra maple syrup&lt;br&gt;
• Optional: bee pollen, hemp seeds, chia, or anything crunchy + nourishing&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Instructions&lt;br&gt;
Night Before&lt;br&gt;
	1.	Combine: In a jar with a lid, add the coconut milk, almond milk, tahini, cinnamon, maple syrup, salt, and steel cut oats.&lt;br&gt;
	2.	Shake: Seal and give it a good shake.&lt;br&gt;
	3.	Chill: Refrigerate overnight to thicken.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Note: You can skip the maple syrup and tahini in the mixture if you prefer to add them as toppings — I often do this. The base can simply be milk, cinnamon, and salt.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Morning Of&lt;br&gt;
	1.	Heat: Pour the porridge into a small saucepan over medium heat until warm. (Microwave works too if you’re short on time.)&lt;br&gt;
	2.	Serve: Transfer to a bowl.&lt;br&gt;
	3.	Top: Add berries, a drizzle of tahini or nut butter, maple syrup to taste, and any extras you love. The tahini + blueberries combo is heaven.&lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;
Save this so you can already wake up nourished and grounded. &lt;br&gt;
&lt;br&gt;

			<img src="https://marinmamacooks.com/wp-content/plugins/instagram-feed-pro/img/placeholder.png" alt="Creamy Overnight Steel Cut Oats for One (5-Minute Prep)
Serves 1
I love making my breakfast at night, so my mornings feel grounded and calm. It takes the guesswork out of ‘what’s for breakfast?’ and this one takes under 5 minutes to prep — and just 5 minutes to heat up.

Ingredients
For the Porridge Base
• ½ cup unsweetened full-fat canned coconut milk 
• ¼ cup unsweetened almond milk (or any milk you love) @threetreesfoods 
• ½ tablespoon raw, smooth tahini
• ½ teaspoon cinnamon (I use Ceylon)
• 1 teaspoon pure maple syrup
• Pinch of pink Himalayan Sea salt
• ¼ cup gluten-free steel cut oats (or rolled oats)

Suggested Toppings
• Drizzle of tahini, almond butter, walnut butter, or peanut butter
• 1 cup frozen wild blueberries (thawed), or any berries
• Extra maple syrup
• Optional: bee pollen, hemp seeds, chia, or anything crunchy + nourishing

Instructions
Night Before
	1.	Combine: In a jar with a lid, add the coconut milk, almond milk, tahini, cinnamon, maple syrup, salt, and steel cut oats.
	2.	Shake: Seal and give it a good shake.
	3.	Chill: Refrigerate overnight to thicken.

Note: You can skip the maple syrup and tahini in the mixture if you prefer to add them as toppings — I often do this. The base can simply be milk, cinnamon, and salt.

Morning Of
	1.	Heat: Pour the porridge into a small saucepan over medium heat until warm. (Microwave works too if you’re short on time.)
	2.	Serve: Transfer to a bowl.
	3.	Top: Add berries, a drizzle of tahini or nut butter, maple syrup to taste, and any extras you love. The tahini + blueberries combo is heaven.

Save this so you can already wake up nourished and grounded.

						entries.forEach( ( entry ) => {

								let lazyloadBackground = entry.target;
								if( lazyloadBackground ) {
									lazyloadBackground.classList.add( 'e-lazyloaded' );
								}
								lazyloadBackgroundObserver.unobserve( entry.target );

					} );
